 Or when the worshipper increases his riches, may not his treasures be locked away.
 4 Or Asura, too, was born from Heaven. You, Varuṇa, are the King of all men.
 The charioteer was well content, forbearing to anger Death with such a great sin.
 This sin was committed by Sakaputa here. Heroes who fled to their dear friend he slew,
 When the Steed brings down your grace and favor in dear and worshipful forms.
 6 Your Mother Aditi, you wise ones, were purified with water, just as the earth is purified from heaven.
 Show love and kindness here below: bathe her in rays of heavenly light.
 7 You two have seated yourselves as Lords of Wealth, as one mounts a chariot to the one who sits on the pole, on the wood.
 These our disheartened tribes, Nrmadas, saved from sorrow, Sumadas saved from sorrow.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXIII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10133.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Sing strength to Indra so he can take his chariot to the front.
Giver of space in tight battles, slayer of enemies in the clash of war, be our great supporter. May the weak bows break on the bows of feeble enemies.

2. You destroyed the Dragon; you sent the rivers down to earth.
Foeless, O Indra, you were born. You care for every choice thing. That’s why we draw close to you. May the weak bows break on the bows of feeble enemies.

3. All malignities and our enemy’s plans be destroyed.
Your bolt you cast at the foe, O Indra, who would strike us dead: your generous bounty gives us wealth.

4. The bandits around us, Indra, who watch and aim at us—
Trample them underfoot; you are a conqueror who scatters them.
5. Whoever attacks us, Indra, be the man a stranger or related,
Bring down his strength, even if it’s as vast as the sky.

6. We cling to your friendship, O Indra, whether we’re dependent on you or not.
Lead us beyond all pain and grief along the path of holy Law.

7. Bestow upon us this, O Indra, who yields according to the singer’s wish,
That the great Cow may, with an endless udder, pour out a thousand streams, giving milk to feed us.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXIV. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10134.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Like the morning sun, O Indra, you have filled both the earth and the sky.
Just as the mighty one, the great king of all powerful beings, the goddess mother gave birth to you, and the blessed mother gave you life.
2. Crush the stubborn strength of mortals whose hearts are set on wickedness.
Smash them under your feet who watch for and aim at us. The goddess mother gave birth to you, and the blessed mother gave you life.
3. Shake down, O slayer of foes, those great, splendid enemies.
With all your powers, O Śakra, and all your helpers, O Indra, shake them down:
4. Just as you, O Śatakratu, and O Indrv, shake everything down,
Give wealth to the one who pours out the juice, with your help, make it tenfold.
5. Let lightning flashes fall around us, everywhere like drops of sweat.
May all malice pass away from us like threads of Darva grass.
6. You hold in your hand a spear like a long hook, great counselor!
As a goat draws down its branch with its front foot, bring down the branch, O Maghavan.
7. Never, O gods, do we offend, and we never are obstinate; we walk as holy texts command.
We clasp and cling to you, cling to your sides, beneath your arms.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXV. Yama.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10135.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. In the tree adorned with lush leaves where Yama drinks with the gods,
The Father, Master of the house, nurtures with love our ancient ancestors.
2. I looked at him who cherishes those old men,  
At him who walks the dark path and then I long for this again.
3. You ride, though unseen, Child, in the new, wheelless chariot
That you have crafted mentally, one-poled yet turning every way.
4. The chariot you've made to roll hitherward from the sages, Child!
This has the Sāman followed close, hence, laid together on a ship.
5. Who was the father of the child? Who made the chariot roll away?
Who will this day declare to us how the funeral gift was made?
6. When the funeral gift was placed, straightaway the flame appeared.
A depth extended in the front: a passage out was made behind.
7. Here is the seat where Yama dwells, what's called the home of gods:
Here minstrels blow the flute for him, here he is glorified with songs.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXVI. Kesins.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10136.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. He with the long, loose hair supports Agni, and moisture, heaven, and earth:
 He is all sky to look upon; he with long hair is called this light.
2. The Munis, wrapped in the wind, wear yellow-hued garments.
 They, following the wind’s swift course, go where the Gods have gone before.
3. Transported with our Munihood, we have pressed on into the winds:
 You therefore, mortal men, behold our natural bodies and no more.
4. The Muni, joined in the holy work of every God,
 Looks upon all varied forms and flies through the region of the air.
5. The Steed of Vāta, Vāyu’s friend, the Muni, driven by the Gods,
 Has his home in both the oceans, in eastern and western seas.
6. Treading the path of sylvan beasts, Gandharvas, and Apsarases,
 He with long locks, who knows the wish, is a sweet, delightful friend.
7. Vāyu has churned for him; for him he pounds the hardest things to bend,
 When he with long loose locks drinks, with Rudra, water from the cup.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXVII Viśvedevas.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10137.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Oh gods, lift up once more the person you've made weak and fallen.
2. Oh gods, bring back to life the one who has committed a sin.
3. Hither, O Wind, bring healing balm, blow away all disease, you Wind;
For you, who carry all medicine, come as the gods' envoy.
4. I am near to you with balms to soothe you and keep you safe.
I bring you strength, I drive away your weakening ailment.
5. Let the gods deliver him, let the Maruts' band deliver him:
All things that exist deliver him so he's free from his disease.
6. The waters have their healing power; the waters drive disease away.
The waters have a balm for everything; let them make medicine for you.
7. The tongue that guides the voice leads first. Then with our ten-fingered hands,
With these two disease-chasers we gently touch you.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXVIII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10138.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. ALLIED with you in friendship, Indra, these priests remember Holy Law, tearing apart Vṛtra limb by limb,
 When they gave birth to the Dawn and let the waters flow, and when you punished the dragons called at Kutsa’s call.
 2 You sent forth fruitful powers, cleaved the hills, drove the cattle forward, and drank the sweet Soma.
 You gave growth through this Tree’s extraordinary might. The Sun shone under the hymn that sprang from Holy Law.
 3 In the middle of the sky, the Sun yoked his chariot; the Arya found a match to face his demon foe.
 Join forces with Rishi Indra who overthrew the solid fortresses of Pipru, conjuring Asuras.
 4 He bravely brought down fortresses no one had ever attacked; tireless he destroyed the godless treasures.
 Like the Sun and Moon, he took the stronghold’s wealth away, and, praised in song, defeated enemies with a flashing spear.
 5 Armed with invincible weapons, with immense power to split, the Vṛtra-slayer sharpens his arrows and deals deadly blows.
 Bright Uṣas was afraid of Indra’s killing bolt; she went on her way and left her chariot behind.
 6 These are your celebrated deeds, only yours, when you alone left the others without sacrifice.
 You set the order of the Moons in the heavens; the Father bears the portioned-out gifts by you.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXXXIX. Savitar.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10139.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. SAVITAR, golden-haired, has raised the east with its radiant beams; he shines eternally in his power.
 He who guides Pūṣan, the wise one, oversees all existence like a herdsman.

2. He sits amidst the heavens that fill the two halves of the world, surveying the vast expanse of the sky and air.

3. He, the source of wealth, gathers treasures with his might, looking at every form and figure.

 Savitar, like a god whose law is constant, stands in the battle for the spoils like Indra.

4. Waters from the sacrifice came to Visvavasu, O Soma, when they saw him. Indra, seeing them off, looked around at the Sun's enclosures.

5. Visvavasu shall sing this song for us, the meter of the celestial Gandharva in the middle realm of the air.
 May we know truth and falsehood well, and may he inspire our thoughts and aid our praises.

6. In the path of the floods, he found the plunderer; he opened the rocky cow-pen's doors with Amṛta.
 These, the Gandharva told him, were rowed by dragons. Indra knew well the prowess of the dragons.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXL. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10140.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Agni, life and glory are yours; your flames burn brightly, you are rich in radiant beams!
 Sage, shining bright, you give to the worshipper, with strength, the food that deserves praise.

2. With brilliant, purifying shine, with perfect shine you lift yourself in light.
 You visit both your Mothers, as a son, you join the earth and sky together.

3. O Jātavedas, Son of Strength, rejoice in our fair hymns and songs.
 In you are stored various forms of nourishment, born noble and of great help.

4. Agni, spread forth, as Ruler, over living things: give wealth to us, Immortal God.
 You shine from a fair sight to behold: you lead us to victorious power.

5. To him, the wise, who orders sacrifice, who has great riches under his control,
 You give blessed reward of good, and plentiful food, give him wealth that conquers all.

6. The men have set before them for their welfare Agni, strong, visible to all, the Holy.
 You, Godlike One, with ears to hear, men’s generations magnify with praise-songs.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLI. Viśvedevas.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10141.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Come, Agni, speak to us kindly; join with us in good will.
Enrich us, Master of the home; you are the Giver of our wealth.
2. May Aryaman grant us wealth, and Bhaga, and Bṛhaspati.
May the gods give their gifts, and Sūnṛtā, Goddess, bless us with wealth.
3. We call King Soma to our aid, and Agni with our songs and hymns,
Ādityas, Viṣṇu, Sūrya, and the Brahman Priest Bṛhaspati.
4. Indra, Vāyu, Bṛhaspati, swift to hear, we invoke,
That all folk in council may be kind to us.
5. Urge Aryaman to send us gifts, and Indra, and Bṛhaspati,
Vāta, Viṣṇu, Sarasvatī, and the Strong Courser Savitar.
6. You, Agni, with your fires, strengthen our prayer and sacrifice:
Urge givers to bestow their wealth to aid our service of the gods.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLII. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10142.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. WITH YOU, AGNI, I sing this hymn; you are my only kin, O Strong One.
 You provide a triple-guarded shelter. Keep the destructive lightning far from us.

2. The one who seeks sustenance in the falling waters, Agni, is your birthplace. As your companion, you win all living beings.

 Our horses and our songs will be victorious. They move forward like a herdsman guarding his herd.

3. And you, Agni, with divine nature, spare the stones while gathering the brushwood.
 Then your tracks will be like deserts in the fields. May we not anger your mighty arrow.

4. Over hills and valleys, devouring as you pass, you divide like an army eager for plunder.
 Like a barber shaves a beard, you shave the earth as the wind blows on your flame and fans it.

5. His lines are apparent as he approaches; the course is single, but the chariots are many.
 Agni, as you advance over the land beneath you, make your arms resplendent and let all the Vasus sit beside you.

6. Let your strength and burning flames rise upward, your energies, Agni, as you work.

 Gape widely, bend yourself, growing stronger. Let all the Vasus be here today beside you.

7. This is the waters' reservoir, the great dwelling of gathered streams.
 Take another path and walk as you please.
 
8. Let the flowers of Durva grow on your path as you come and go.
 Let there be lakes with lotus blooms. These are the mansions of the flood.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLIII. Aśvins.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10143.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. You created Atri, who was old but still agile, like a horse eager to reach its goal.
When you rejuvenated Kakṣīvān, making him strong and youthful again,
2. You freed Atri, as if he were born anew, and brought him back to Earth.
You loosened the tight knot that the gods had tied, unsoiled by dust.
3. Warriors who displayed the greatest wonder to Atri, strive to earn beautiful songs;
For then, O Sky Warriors, your praise will never cease.

4. This calls to you, Generous Gods! - oblation, Aśvins! And our love,
That you, O Warriors, in battle may bring us safely to a spacious place.

5. You two, tossed in the ocean at the ends of the world,
Nāsatyas, with your winged attendants came close, and gave him strength to win.

6. Come with your joys, most generous Gods, Lords of all wealth, bringing good fortune.
Like fresh water to a well, Heroes come and join us.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLIV. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10144.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. This immortal Indu, like a horse, strong and full of vigor,
Belongs to you, the Orderer.
2. Here, by us, for the worshipper, is the wise bolt that works with skill.
It brings the bubbling Soma as a skilled man brings the potent drink.
3. Impetuous Ahīśuva, a bull among bulls,
looked down upon the restless hawk.
4. That the strong-winged bird brought, Child of the falcon, from afar,
What moves on a hundred wheels along the female dragon’s path.
5. Which, fair and unharmed, the falcon brought to you in its foot,
the red-hued dwelling of the juice;
Through this came vital power that extends our days, and kinship through its help was awakened.
6. So Indra is by Indu’s power; even among gods it will repel great treachery.
Wisdom, Most Wise One, brings strength that extends life. May wisdom bring the Soma to us.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLV. Sapatnibadhanam.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10145.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. I dig up this plant from the earth, a powerful herb that silences rivals,
And makes me the husband while driving them away.
2. Blessed, with wide leaves, sent by the gods, this victorious plant,
Blow away my rival wife and make my husband solely mine.
3. I am stronger, Stronger One, much more powerful than the strongest,
And my rival wife is nothing compared to the lowest dames.
4. I won't even say her name; she doesn't take pleasure in this man.
Drive her far away, into the deepest distance.
5. I am the conqueror, and you too be victorious,
As we both gain victory, we'll subdue my rival wife.
6. I've captured you as my vanquisher, with a stronger spell,
Like a calf hurries to its mother, may your spirit come to me,
Move swiftly like water flowing down its course.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLVI. Aranyani.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10146.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Forest Goddess, you vanish from sight, why don't you seek the village?
Are you afraid?

2. When the grasshopper chirps and the cicada sings,
It seems like tinkling bells, the Forest Goddess rejoices.

3. Cattle seem to graze, and a place seems to appear:
Or perhaps at dusk, the Forest Goddess frees the wagons.

4. One calls to his cow, another fells a tree,
At dusk, the woodland dweller thinks someone has screamed.

5. The Goddess never kills, unless a murderous foe approaches.
Man eats the fragrant fruit and rests as he pleases.

6. I have praised the Forest Queen, sweet-smelling, fragrant with balm,
Mother of all forest things, she neither farms nor stores, yet has plenty.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLVII Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10147.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. I trust in your first fierce deed, O Indra, when you slew Vṛtra and brought benefit to mankind;
 When the two halves of the world fell short of you in strength, and the earth trembled under your might, O Thunderbolt.

2. You with your magical powers tore apart the magician Vṛtra, O Blameless One, with a heart that craved fame.
 Heroes choose you when they fight for the prize, you in all sacrifices worthy of praise.

3. Lord Much-invoked, take pleasure in these princes here, who, your exalters, Maghavan, have come to wealth.
 In assemblies, when the ritual succeeds, they sing the praises of the Strong for sons and offspring and untroubled riches.

4. The man who finds joy in well-guarded wealth, whose care brings him the sought-after happy drink, will bring offerings, Maghavan, with you, swiftly win the spoils with heroes in the fray.

5. Now for our company, O Maghavan, when praised, make ample space with might, and grant us riches.
 You, Magician, our Varuṇa and Mitra, provide food to us, O Wondrous one, as Distributor.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLVIII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10148.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. When we press the juice, we praise you, Indra, and when we win the spoils, we are most valiant.
Bring us prosperity, so that each of us can achieve what they desire under your protection, may we conquer.

2. Born sublime, oh Indra, Hero, with Surya, may you subdue the Dāsa races.
As at a fountain's edge, we bring the Soma hidden deep within the waters.

3. Answer the hymn-singer’s songs, for you know them, seeking the Ṛṣis' prayer, yourself a singer.
May we be the ones who enjoy the Soma: these with sweet offerings, O Chariot-rider.

4. These holy prayers, O Indra, I sing for you; grant to the men the strength of men, you Hero.
Be of one mind with those you joy, keep the singers safe and their companions.

5. Listen to Pṛthi's call, heroic Indra, and be praised by Venya's hymns.
He who has sung you to your oil-rich home, whose rolling songs have made you swift as a torrent.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXLIX. Savitar.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10149.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Savitar fixed the earth with bands to bind it, and made heaven stedfast where no prop supported.
 Savitar milked the wind, as if it were a restless horse, tethering the air and sea to what no foot had touched.

2. Savitar, Child of Waters, well knows where the ocean, firmly fixed, overflows its limits.
 There arose the world from there; from there heaven spread out and the wide earth expanded.

3. With a full company of immortal beings, this other realm came later, high and holy.
 First indeed, Savitar’s eagle with strong wings was born; and he obeys his law forever.

4. As warriors to their steeds, cows to their villages, as loving mothers bring forth calves,
 May Savitar come down to us, heaven’s bearer, Lord of all blessings.

5. Like the Aṅgirasa Hiranvastupa, I invoke you, Savitar, to this achievement:
 Thus worshipping and praising you for your favor, I watch for you as for the Soma stalk.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CL. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10150.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. You, who receive offerings, you who are lit up, are lit up for the gods.
With the Ādityas, Rudras, and Vasus, come to us: to grant us favor, come to us.

2. Come here and accept with joy this sacrifice and hymn of ours.
Oh kindled God, we mortals invoke you, calling on you to show us favor.

3. I praise you, Jātavedas, Lord of all good things, with my song.
Agni, bring the gods whose laws we love, whose laws we love, to show us favor.

4. Agni, the god, was made the great high-priest of the gods, Rishis kindled Agni, men of mortal form.
Agni, I invoke for winning abundant wealth. Kindly disposed for winning wealth.

5. Atri and Bharadvāja and Gavisthira, Kaṇva and Trasadasyu, in our fight they aided.
On Agni calls Vasiṣṭha, the household priest, to win his favor.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLI. Faith.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10151.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Through faith, Agni is lit, and through faith, offerings are made.
We praise faith on the heights of joy.
2. May you bless the giver, O faith; may faith bless the one who wishes to give.
Bless those generous worshipers; bless the words I've spoken.
3. Just as the gods upheld faith in the powerful demons,
May this wish I utter be true for the generous worshipers.
4. Protected by Vayu, gods and men who perform sacrifices come close to faith.
One wins faith through heartfelt desires and wealth through faith.
5. May we invoke faith in the morning, faith at midday,
And faith at sunset. O faith, grant us belief.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10152.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. You are a mighty governor, wondrous, destroyer of enemies,
 Whose friends never die, and never are defeated.
 2 Lord of the clan, who brings us joy, strong, warrior, slayer of demons,
 May India, Soma drinker, lead us on, bull who grants us peace.
 3 Drive away demons and foes, shatter Vṛtra’s jaws:
 O Vṛtra slayer, quell the man’s anger who threatens us.
 4 O Indra, drive away our enemies, humble those who dare to challenge us:
 Send down to the underworld him who seeks to harm us.
 5 Foil the enemy’s plan, guard against his weapon that would conquer us.
 Keep his furious rage at bay and shield us from his deadly dart.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLIII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10153.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. The powerful ones approached Indra at his birth, sharing his great strength.
 And you, mighty one, are truly strong.
 2 You were born based on strength, victory, and power, O Indra.
 You, mighty one, are indeed strong.
 3 You are the slayer of Vṛtra, Indra, and you spread the sky:
 You upheld the heavens with might.
 4 You, Indra, carry the lightning that suits you,
 Sharpening your thunderbolt with might.
 5 You, Indra, are supreme over all creatures in your might:
 You pervade every place.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLIV. New Life.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10154.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Some drink Soma purified, some sit by sacrificial oil:
 To those whose mead flows freely, even to those let him depart.
 2 Invincible through fervor, those who fervor brought to heaven,
 Who showed great fervor in their lives— even to those let him depart.
 3 Warriors who fight bravely and lay down their lives,
 Or who give a thousand-fold reward— even to those let him depart.
 4 Yes, the first followers of law, law’s pure and holy protectors,
 The Fathers, Yama! Fervor-moved, even to those let him depart.
 5 Skilled in a thousand ways and means, the sages who protect the Sun,
 The Rishis, Yama! Fervor-moved— even to those let him depart.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLV. Various.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10155.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. ARAYI, one-eyed limping hag, fly, ever-screeching, to the hill.
We frighten you away with these, the heroes of Sirimbitha.
2. Scared from this place and that is she, destroyer of each germ unborn.
Go, sharp-horned Brāhmaṇaspti and drive Arayi far away.
3. That floating log without a man to guide it on the river’s edge—
Seize it, you thing with hideous jaws, and go you far away thereon.
4. When, foul with secret stain and spot, you hastened onward to the breast,
All Indra’s enemies were slain and passed away like froth and foam.
5. These men have led about the cow, have duly carried Agni round,
And raised their glory to the Devas. Who will attack them with success?


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLVI. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10156.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. LET our songs send Agni racing like a swift horse in the race,
And we'll win every prize through him.
2. Agni, the spear that brings us cows for ourselves with your help,
That sends us wealth for what we seek.
3. O Agni, bring us secure wealth, vast wealth in horses and in cows:
Oil you the axle, turn the wheel.
4. O Agni, you've made the Sun, the Eternal Star, rise in the sky,
Bestowing light upon living men.
5. You, Agni, are the people’s light, best, dearest, in your shrine:
Watch over the singer, give him life.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLVII. Viśvedevas.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10157.htm
--------------------------------------------------
We will bring these existing worlds under Indra's and all the gods' control.

Our sacrifice, our bodies, and our offspring. May Indra join them with the Adityas.

With the Adityas, with the group of Maruts, may Indra protect our bodies.

As when the gods arrived, after they had slain the Asuras and kept their divine nature,
They brought the Sun hitherward with great power and beheld their vigorous divinity.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLVIII. Sūrya.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10158.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. MAY Surya protect us from heaven, and Vāta from the sky,
 And Agni from the earth.
 2 Thou Savitar whose fire deserves a hundred libations, be thou pleased:
 From failing lightning keep us safe.
 3 May Savitar the God and Parvata also grant us sight;
 May the Creator grant us sight.
 4 Grant sight to our eyes, grant sight to our bodies so they may see:
 May we survey and understand this world.
 5 Thus, Surya, may we behold you, the most beautiful to see,
 See clearly with human eyes.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLIX. Saci Paulomi.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10159.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Surya has risen high, and this my happy fate I have achieved.
 Knowing this, as a conqueror, I have won my husband for myself.
 2 I am the banner and the head, a mighty ruler I am:
 I am victorious, and my Lord shall be submissive to my will.
 3 My sons are slayers of the enemy, my daughter rules as queen:
 I am victorious; my song of triumph is supreme over my Lord.
 4 Offering, that which Indra gave and thus grew glorious and most high—
 I have offered this, oh gods, and rid me of each rival wife.
 5 Destroyer of the rival wife, sole spouse, victorious, conqueror,
 I have seized the glory of others as if it were the wealth of weaker women.
 6 I have subdued as conqueror these rivals, these my fellow-wives,
 That I may hold imperial sway over this Hero and the folk.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLX. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10160.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Drink this potent elixir filled with offerings: harness your horses here and now.
 Don't let those other sacrificers hold you back, Indra: these juices are ready for you.
 2 You have the juice that flows, and more that will flow: our resounding songs invite you.
 Oh Indra, pleased by this libation today, come, you who know all and drink the Soma.
 3 Whoever, devoted to the God, offers Soma with a longing heart and soul—
 Indra never gives away his cattle: for him he makes the Soma famous.
 4 He looks with loving favor on the mortal who, like a rich man, pours Soma for him.
 The mighty one supports him with his bended arm: he slays without being asked those who hate devotion.
 5 We call upon you to join us, eager for goods and spoils, for cattle and horses.
 For your new love and favor, we are here: let us invoke you, Indra, for our well-being.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXI. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10161.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. FOR life I offer you this sacrifice from the end of days and from Death;
 Or, if that greedy demon has taken hold of him, free him from it, O Indra, and Agni.
 2 May his days be over, may he now be gone, may he be close to death already,
 Back from Destruction’s embrace I bring him, save him so he lives a hundred autumns.
 3 With a hundred-eyed offering, a hundred-year-old one, giving a hundred lives, I restore him,
 That Indra may lead him safely for a hundred years to the far side of all misfortune.
 4 Live, growing stronger, a hundred autumns, live through a hundred springs, a hundred winters.
 By a hundred-lived offering Indra, Agni, Brihaspathi, Savitar, I give him a hundred!
 5 Thus have I found and saved you, you have returned with renewed youth.
 Entire in your body! I have found your sight and all your life for you.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXII. Agni
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10162.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. May Agni, who answers our prayer, the rakṣasa slayer, drive away
the illness of a bad name that has plagued your laboring womb.
2. Agni, joining with the prayer, drive off the flesh-eater,
the illness of a bad name that has attacked your baby and womb.
3. That which destroys the sinking seed, the settled, moving embryo,
that which will kill the baby at birth—let us drive it far away.
4. That which divides your legs so they can lie between the couple,
and penetrates and licks your side—let us eradicate it.
5. Whatever rests by you in borrowed form of brother, lover, or lord,
and wants to destroy your offspring—let us eradicate it.
6. That which, through sleep or darkness, has deceived you and lies by you,
and will destroy your offspring—let us eradicate it.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXIII
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10163.htm
--------------------------------------------------
From both your nostrils, from your eyes, from your ears, and from your chin,
I drive away your ailment with this mantra.

2. From your neck tendons and neck, from your ribcage and spine,
From your shoulders, upper and lower arms, I drive away your ailment.

3. From your internal organs and all within, from your anus,
From your heart, kidneys, liver, and spleen, I drive away your ailment.

4. From your thighs, from your knees, and from your heels, and from your feet,
From your hips, from your stomach, and from your groin, I drive away your ailment.

5. From whatever is excreted from within, and from your hair, and from your nails,
From all of you from head to toe, I drive away your ailment.

6. From every part, every hair, disease that enters every joint,
From all of you, from head to toe, I drive away your ailment.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXIV. Dream-charm.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10164.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. DEPART, you Master of the mind, go far away.
Look upon destruction far from here. The living mind has many paths.

2. Men choose a great blessing, a happy boon they gain.
They see bliss with Vaivasvata. The living mind seeks many places.

3. If, by addressing, blaming, or cursing, we commit sin—awake or asleep—
All hateful deeds and evil actions may Agni carry off to distant lands.

4. May Indra, Brahmāṇaspathi, prevent our foes from troubling us,
When our deeds are wrong and unjust.

5. We have triumphed today and freed ourselves from sin and guilt.
Ill thoughts, whether awake or asleep, seize the man we hate, yes, the man who hates us.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXV. Viśvedevas.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10165.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. DEITIES, whatever dove came seeking us, sent by you as the messenger of destruction,
 For this let us sing hymns and make atonement. May it be well with our quadrupeds and bipeds.
2. May the auspicious dove that has been sent to us, a harmless bird, O DEITIES, within our home.
 May Agni, Sage, be pleased with our offering, and may the missile-bearing dove avoid us.
3. Let not the arrow-winged dove distract us: beside the fireplace, on the hearth it settles.
 May it bring welfare to our men and cattle: here let the dove, O DEITIES, refrain from harming us.
4. The screeching of the owl is ineffective, and when the dove has settled beside the fire,
 To him who sent it hither as a messenger, to him be reverence, to Death, to Yama.
5. Drive forth the dove, chase it with holy verses: rejoicing, bring ye hither food and cattle,
 Barred against all grief and trouble. Let the swift bird fly forth and leave us strength.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXVI. Sapatnanāśanam.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10166.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. MAKE me a bull among my peers, make me my rivals, conqueror:
 Make me the slayer of my foes, a sovran ruler, lord of kine.
2. I am my rivals’ slayer, like Indra unwounded and unhurt,
 And all these enemies of mine are vanquished and beneath my feet.
3. Here, verily, I bind you fast, as the two bow-ends with the string.
 Press down these men, O Lord of Speech, that they may humbly speak to me.
4. Hither I came as conqueror with mighty all-effecting power,
 And I have mastered all your thought, your synod, and your holy work.
5. May I be highest, having gained your strength in war, your skill in peace
 my feet have trodden on your heads.
 Speak to me from beneath my feet, as frogs from out the water croak, as frogs from out the water croak.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXVII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10167.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. This pleasing drink, O Indra, we offer you; you are the ruler of cups and nectar.
Bestow upon us wealth with many brave sons; you, glowing with passion, won heavenly light.

2. Let us invoke Śakra with this libation, the one who wins with light and delights in potent nectar.
Watch over our sacrifice, come to us then; we pray to Maghavan, the conqueror of armies.

3. By the decree of royal Soma and Varuṇa, under Bṛhaspati and Anumati’s protection,
Today under your authority, O Maghavan, Creator, Arranger, I have enjoyed the jars.

4. I too, urged on, had my share, in the bowl, and as the first prince, I composed this hymn of praise,
When I reached the flowing nectar, O Vīsavāmītra, Jamadagni, to your home.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXVIII. Vāyu.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10168.htm
--------------------------------------------------
O Wind’s chariot, its might and splendor! It roars and shakes with a thunderous sound.
It colors the lands and touches the heavens, and as it moves, it stirs the dust of the earth.
Along the Wind’s tracks, they hurry along, they gather to him like ladies at a gathering.
Borne by his chariot with them as his attendants, the God swiftly travels, the ruler of the universe.
Travelling on the air’s middle path, no single day does he rest or sleep.
Holy and firstborn, friend of the waters, where did he spring and from what region did he come?
Germ of the world, the vital spirit of the Deities, this God moves ever as his will directs him.
His voice is heard, his form is ever unseen. Adore this Wind with our offering.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXIX. COWS.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10169.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. May the wind blow upon our cows with healing; may they eat grass full of robust juices.
May they drink water rich in life and richness; to food that moves on feet be gracious, Rudra.
2. Like-colored, various-hued, or single-colored, whose names through sacrifice are known to Agni,
Whom the Aṅgirases produced by fervor—vouchsafe to these, Parjanya, great protection.
3. Those who have offered their bodies to the gods, whose varied forms are all well-known to Soma—
Those grant us in our cattle pen, O Indra, with their full streams of milk and plentiful offspring.
4. Prajāpati, bestowing these upon me, one-minded with all gods and with the fathers,
Has brought to our cattle pen auspicious cattle; may we own the offspring they will bear us.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXX. Sūrya.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10170.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. May the Bright One drink this sacred Soma, granting the sacrifice’s lord an unharmed life;
 He who, driven by the wind, protects our children well, has fed them and shines over many lands.

2. Radiant, like high Truth, cherished, the mightiest to gain power, Truth based on the law that upholds the heavens,
 He rose as light that vanquishes Vṛtras and foes, the best slayer of Dasyus, Asuras, and enemies.

3. This light, the best of lights, supreme, all-conquering, rich-winner, is praised with high praise.
 All-lighting, radiant, mighty as the Sun to behold, it spreads unfailing victory and strength.

4. With your light, you have reached heaven’s luminous realm.
 Through you all existing things were gathered together, possessor of all divinity, All-Effecting God.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXI. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10171.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. FOR Iṭa's sake you pressed the juice, Indra, you protected his chariot,
 And heard the Soma-bearer’s call.
2. You bore the head of the swift warrior from his skin,
 And sought the Soma-offerer’s home.
3. Venya, that mortal man, you many times set free,
 O Indra, for Āstrabudhna the devout.
4. Bring, Indra, the Sun back to the east,
 Even against the gods’ will.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXII. Dawn.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10172.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. COME ALL BEAUTIFUL WITH YOUR FULL UDDERS: THE KINE FOLLOW ON YOUR PATH WITH KIND THOUGHTS.
 2 COME WITH MERCIFUL THOUGHTS AND ROAR A WAR-HYMN OF PRAISE, BOUNTIOUSLY OFFERING SACRIFICE.
 3 AS NOURISHERS WE TIE THE THREAD, AND, BOUNTIOUS WITH OUR BOUNTY, WE OFFER SACRIFICE.
 4 DAWN DRIVES AWAY HER SISTER'S GLOOM AND MAKES HER RETRACE HER PATH THROUGH HER EXCELLENCE.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXIII. The King.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10173.htm
--------------------------------------------------
Be with us; I have chosen you: stand steadfast and unmoving.
Let all the people wish for you, let your kingship not fall away.
Be even here; do not fall away, be like a mountain unremoved.
Stand steadfast here like Indra himself, and hold the kingship in your grasp.

This man has Indra established, made secure by strong oblations' power.
May Soma bless him, and Brahmāṇaspati, on him.
The sky is firm, the earth is firm, and these hills are also steadfast.
All this living world is steadfast, and this King of men is also steadfast.

Steadfast, may Varuṇa the King, steadfast, the God Bṛhaspati,
Steadfast, may Indra, steadfast too, may Agni keep your steadfast reign.

Think of constant Soma with constant sacrifice,
And then may Indra make the clans bring tribute only to you.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXIV. The King.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10174.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. FOR victory in battle, may Indra help us win.
 With this, O Brahmāṇaspati, may we gain royal power.
 2 To subdue our rivals, to crush all evil,
 Against anyone who threatens us, against anyone who angers us.
 3 May Soma and Savitar bless you as a victorious king,
 All elements have helped you, to make you a conqueror.
 4 May this oblation, which Indra gave and thus became glorious and great,
 Be mine, Gods! And thus, truly, I shall be unmatched.
 5 As slayer of my rivals, I will be unrivaled, victorious,
 May I rule over these beings, may I be the sovereign of the people.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXV. Press-stones.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10175.htm
--------------------------------------------------
May Savitar the Deva, O Stones, stir you according to the Yajna:
Harness yourselves and press.
2. Stones, drive calamity away, drive away malevolence:
Make the Cows our medicine.
3. Together, all the upper Stones, giving the Bull his bull-like strength,
Look down with pride on those below.
4. May Savitar the Deva, O Stones, stir you as Yajna commands
For him who sacrifices, pouring juice.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXVI. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10176.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. THEIR SONS HAVE TOLD ALONG THE RUBHUS' MIGHTY DEEDS IN HYMNS OF PRAISE.
Who, all-supporting, have enjoyed the earth as if it were a mother cow.
2. Bring forth the God with divine song, being Jātavedas hitherward,
To bear our gifts to heaven at once.
3. Here, a God-devoted Priest leads forward to the sacrifice,
Like a chariot covered for the road, he, glowing, knows his own way.
4. This Agni rescues from distress, as if from the Immortal Race,
A God mightier than strength, a God made for life.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXVII. Māyābheda.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10177.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. The wise see the bird adorned with all a demon’s magical power. Sages observe it in the ocean’s deepest part; the wise finders seek the spot where its beams shine.
2. The flying bird carries speech within its spirit. Before, the Gandharva spoke it in the womb. At the sacrificial seat, the sages cherish this radiant, heavenly-bright invention.
3. I saw the herdsman, who never rests, coming and going along his paths. He, cloaked in gathered and diffused brilliance, continually travels through the worlds.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXVIII. Tārkṣya.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10178.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. This very powerful one, whom the gods command, the conqueror of chariots, ever victorious,
Swift and swift-footed, with unharmed feet, even Tārkṣya for our benefit, we call him here.
2. As if we offer our gifts to Indra, may we ascend him as a ship for safety.
Like the two vast worlds, wide and deep, may we be safe both when he arrives and departs.
3. He who has spread his might across the Five Lands, like Sūrya with his radiance, and the waters—
His strength wins hundreds, none can turn it back, as a young maiden stands firm against her lover.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXIX. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10179.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Now raise your spirits and behold Indra’s timely portion.
If it’s ready, make the offering; if not, you’ll be excused.
2. The sacrifice is prepared; come, Indra; the Sun has traversed half his path.
Friends with their provisions sit around you, like clan lords awaiting the wandering chief of the tribe.
3. Dressed in milk and aflame, I imagine; this new gift seems well-prepared.
Indra, drink of the noon’s libation’s curds with favor, Thunderer, whose deeds are great.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXX. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10180.htm
--------------------------------------------------
O Much-Invoked One, you have conquered your enemies; your power is supreme. Here, show your bounty.
In your right hand, O Indra, bring us wealth; you are the Lord of rivers filled with riches.
Like a fearsome wild beast roaming on the mountains, you came to us from afar.
Sharpening your brave and sharp sword, O Indra, crush the enemy and scatter those who hate us.
Thou, mighty Indra, sprang into being as strength for a beautiful dominion over the people.
You drove off the folk who were unfriendly, and gave the gods space and freedom.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXI. Viśvedevas.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10181.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. VASIṢṭha mastered the Rathantara, took it from radiant Dhātar, Savitar, and Viṣṇu,
   Offering, part of the fourfold offering, known as Saprathas and Prathas.
2. These sages found what lay remote and hidden, the sacrifice’s loftiest secret essence.
   From radiant Dhātar, Savitar, and Viṣṇu, from Agni, Bharadvāja brought the Brhat.
3. They found with mental eyes the earliest Yajus, a pathway to the Gods, that had descended.
   From radiant Dhātar, Savitar, and Viṣṇu, from Surya did these sages bring the Gharma.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXII. Bṛhaspati.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10182.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. **Bṛhāspati** lead us safely over troubles and turn his evil thoughts against the sinner;  
Repel the curse, and drive away ill-feeling, and give the sacrificer peace and comfort!

2. May **Narāśasma** aid us at Prayāja: blessed be our Anuyāja at invocations.  
May he repel the curse, and chase ill-feeling, and give the sacrificer peace and comfort.

3. May he whose head is blazing burn the demons, haters of prayer, so that the arrow slays them.  
May he repel the curse and chase ill-feeling, and give the sacrificer peace and comfort.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXIII. The Sacrificer, Etc.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10183.htm
--------------------------------------------------
I saw you meditating in your spirit, what sprang from fervor and has developed.
Granting offspring here, granting wealth, spread in your offspring, you who desire children.
I saw you pondering in your heart, praying that your body may be fruitful at the right time.
Come as a youthful woman, rise to meet me: spread in your offspring, you who desire children.
In plants and herbs, in all existing beings, I have laid the seed of growth.
All offspring on earth I have begotten, and sons in women who will be hereafter.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXIV.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10184.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. May Vishnu form the womb, may Tvashtri properly shape the forms,
Prajapati infuse the stream, and Dhatu lay the seed for you.
2. O Sinīvālī, set the seed, set thou the seed, Saraswati:
May the two gods grant the seed, the Aswins crowned with lotuses.
3. That which the two Aswins rub forth with the gold-striking sticks—
That seed of yours we invoke, that in the tenth month you may bear.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXV. Aditi.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10185.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. GREAT, unassailable must he the heavenly favour of Three Devas,
 Varuṇa, Mitra, Aryaman.
 2 O'er these, neither at home nor yet abroad or strange paths,
 The malevolent foe has power.
 3 Nor over him, the man whom Aditi's children bestow Eternal light so he may live.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXVI. Vāyu.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10186.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. May Vāta fill our hearts with health and joy, and grant us long life.
2. You are our father, Vāta, indeed you are also a brother and a friend;
   Grant us strength so that we may live.
3. May we partake of the Amṛta stored away up there, O Vāta, in your home—
   Grant us of it that we may live.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXVII. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10187.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. To Agni I offer this song, the Bull of all the people:
 May he carry us beyond our enemies.
 2 He who shines brilliantly across the wilderness from afar:
 May he carry us beyond our enemies.
 3 The Bull with a bright flame that utterly consumes the demons:
 May he carry us beyond our enemies.
 4 He who sees all that exists and comprehends it with his sight:
 May he carry us beyond our enemies.
 5 Radiant Agni, born in the farthest region of the sky:
 May he carry us beyond our enemies.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXVIII. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10188.htm
--------------------------------------------------
Now send the Jātavedas forth, send the vigorous Steed hitherward  
To sit upon our sacred grass.  
2. I raise the lofty praise of Jātavedas, showering blessings,  
With sages as his heroic band.  
3. With flames of Jātavedas that carry offerings to the Devas,  
May he promote our Yajna.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CLXXXIX. Sūrya.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10189.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. This spotted Bull has arrived, seated before the Mother in the east,
 Proceeding to his Father, heaven.
2. When he expends his breath, she moves across the clear skies:
 The Bull shines through all the heavens.
3. Song is given to the Bird; it rules over thirty realms
 Across the days as dawn breaks.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXC. Creation.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10190.htm
--------------------------------------------------
From fervor raised to its peak, Eternal Law and Truth sprang forth:
Then came Night, and then the ocean's vast expanse.
2. From that same vast ocean of the sea, Year was fashioned next,
Orderer of days and nights, Lord of all who close the eye.
3. Dhātar, the great Creator, then arranged Sun and Moon in order;
He made Heaven and Earth, the regions of the air, and light.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN CXCI. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv10191.htm
--------------------------------------------------
Agni, mighty Agni, gather up all the precious things for your friend.
Bring us all treasures as you burn in the libation’s place.
Assemble, speak together: let your minds be all one.
As ancient Gods sit in unity, let their minds be one.

The place is common, the assembly is common, the mind is common, let your thoughts be united.
I lay a common purpose before you, and offer worship with your general sacrifice.
One and the same be your resolve, and be your minds one.
United be the thoughts of all that all may happily agree.
